God's Transcendence from Parent and Child
Defines God's transcendence from parent and child and refutes Christian doctrines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why rational theology affirms that God cannot have a parent or child, and how this principle refutes Christian claims about Jesus.

Core Idea
God cannot be separated from another being as parent or child.

This lesson addresses two dimensions of God's transcendence: that He has no parent and no child. The text first states the rational impossibility of God being a parent or having offspring, then applies this principle to critique Christian doctrines about Jesus. The argument is based on the nature of God as uncaused and independent, which separates Him from any being that could be a parent or offspring.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the full Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two clear parts: the main text on transcendence and the longer footnote refuting Christian doctrines.
The main text is concise; the footnote expands with a poem.
2
Understand the rational definition
The key idea: God cannot be separated from another living being. This applies both to being a parent (giving birth) and being a child (being born). Reflect on why separation implies contingency.
The impossibility is rational, not merely scriptural.
3
Identify the two aspects
The passage covers two points: no parent (walid) and no child (walad). Note that both are forbidden for the same reason: they involve separation from another being.
4
Examine the Christian refutation
The footnote argues that Jesus having a mother but no father is not impossible (Adam had neither). The poem by Fakhr al-Razi highlights a logical contradiction: if Jesus is divine, why did the Jews overpower him?
Think about how this argument uses rational consistency.
5
Summarize the lesson
Write a one-sentence summary of why God cannot have a parent or child, and how this relates to the Christian claim about Jesus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تَنَزُّهه سبحَانَهُ عن الْوَالِدِ وَالْوَلَدِ
(وَ) حَالَ كونه تعالى مُنزّها عن ( وَالِدٍ) فلا يجوز أنْ يكونَ تعالى مُنفصلا عن حيوان آخر ، أبا كان أو أمَّا ، لصدق الوالد بهما (كَذَا الْوَلَدْ) فيجبُ أَنْ يكون تعالى مُنزّهاً عنه كتَنَزُّهِه عن الوالِد ؛ فلا يجوز أن ينفصل عنه حيوان آخر (٤)
(٤) في هذا الكلام بشقيه - وهما تنزه الباري له عن أن يكون له والِدٌ يَلِدُه ، وعن أنْ يكون له وَلَدٌ ينفصل عنه ـ رَد على النّصارى الذين قالوا بألوهية عيسى فإنهم يعترفون بأنه ابن مريم، وَلَدَتْهُ كما تَلِدُ النساء أولادهم ، والإله لا يكون له والد، ويزعمون أنه ابن الله ، تعالى الله عما يقولون علوا كبيرا ! استكثروا أن يوجَدَ إنسان بغير والد، وقد ضلت حلومهم و عزبت عنهم عقولهم في ذلك ، لأنَّ الله تعالى أوجد آدم من غير أمّ ولا أب، فلأن يقدر سبحانه على إيجاد عيسى مِن أُمّ بلا أب أهونُ وأيسر، وإنَّ مَثَلَ عِيسَى عِندَ اللَّهِ كَمَثَلِ ءَادَمَ خَلَقَهُ مِن تُرَابِ﴾ [آل عمران: ٥٩] . وتنسب إلى الفخر الرازي أبيات في الرد على مقالتهم في عيسى ، وفيها احتجاج على دعواهم ألوهيته مع قولهم إنّ اليهود قتلوه ، وهذه الأبيات هي قوله:
عَجَبًا لِلْمَسِيحِ بَيْنَ النَّصَارَى وإلى الله والدا نَسَبُوه سَلَّمُوهُ إِلَى الْيَهُودِ وَقَالُوا إِنَّهُمْ بَعْدَ قَتْلِهِ صَلَبُوه فَإِذَا كَانَ مَا يَقُولُونَ حَقًّا فَسَلُوهُم وَأَيْنَ كَانَ أَبُوه؟ فإِذَا كَانَ رَاضِيَا بِأَذَاهُمْ فَاشْكُرُوهُمْ لأَجْلِ مَا صَنَعُوه وَإِذَا كَانَ سَاخِطًا بِقَضَاهُمْ فَاعْبُدُوهُمْ لأَنَّهُمْ غَلَبُوه
His transcendence, glory be to Him, from the father and the son. (And) the state of Him, exalted, being transcendent from (a parent), so it is not permissible that He, exalted, be separated from another living being, whether as a father or a mother, because the term parent applies to both; (likewise the offspring), so He, exalted, must be transcendent from it as He is transcendent from the parent; thus it is not permissible that another living being be separated from Him. (4) In this statement with its two parts – which are the transcendence of the Creator from having a parent who gives birth to Him, and from having an offspring that separates from Him – there is a refutation of the Christians who said that Jesus is divine, because they admit that he is the son of Mary, she gave birth to him as women give birth to their children, and the divine cannot have a parent, and they claim that he is the son of God – exalted is God above what they say, a great exaltation! They thought it too much that a human be without a father, and their minds erred and their intellects failed them in that, because God, exalted, created Adam without a mother or father, so that He, glory be to Him, is able to create Jesus from a mother without a father is easier and simpler. 'Indeed, the example of Jesus before God is like that of Adam; He created him from dust' [Qur'an 3:59]. And attributed to Fakhr al-Razi are verses in refutation of their claim about Jesus, in which is an argument against their claim of his divinity while they say that the Jews killed him. These verses are his words: Amazing is the Messiah among the Christians, and to God as a father they attributed him. They handed him over to the Jews and said that after killing him they crucified him. If what they say is true, then ask them: where was his father? If he was content with their harming him, then thank them for what they did. If he was angered by their decree, then worship them because they overcame him.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage covers two aspects of divine transcendence: from having a parent and from having a child. The commentary explains that God cannot be separated from another living being as a father or mother, and likewise cannot have offspring, because that would involve separation from another being. The proof is the same as the proof for God's being different from contingent things. The long footnote provides a refutation of Christian doctrines: it argues that Jesus having a mother but no father is not impossible (since Adam had neither parent), and includes a poem by Fakhr al-Razi that logicizes against the Christian position – if Jesus was divine, why did the Jews overpower him? The poem questions the Christian narrative.

Key Terms
والد
ولد
تَنزيه
نصارى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that God having a parent or child is not impossible if He is omnipotent, because miracles can happen.
Correction: The impossibility is rational and inherent to God's nature as the necessary existent: He cannot be separated from another being, as that would imply He is not self-sufficient.

Checkpoint
What is the main rational reason given for God's transcendence from having a parent or child?
A) It would imply dependence on another being
B) It would imply separation from another living being
C) It would imply a beginning in time
D) It would imply a physical body

Key Takeaway
God's transcendence from parent and child is a necessary rational truth that also refutes false doctrines about Jesus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even for a single moment, imagined God as having some need or dependency? How does the truth that God is absolutely transcendent from any parent or child strip away that subtle anthropomorphism? Will you actively root out such thoughts from your heart?
?
The poem by Fakhr al-Razi shows the absurdity of claiming Jesus is God yet was killed. Is there any area of your life where you act as if God is weak or indifferent to your circumstances, as if He can be overcome? What does this passage call you to change in your trust in Allah's power and transcendence?
?
Christians attributed a son to God. Do you ever compromise the absolute oneness of God by exaggerating the status of a scholar, saint, or leader, even internally? What practical step can you take today to ensure your tawheed remains pure?

God's Transcendence from Having Close Friends
States that God is transcendent from having close friends and gives the proof from His being different from contingents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's uniqueness precludes having close friends, as affirmed by the proof from His being different from contingent beings.

Core Idea
Allah's uniqueness leaves no room for close friends.

The author continues the discussion of divine transcendence by negating any form of close friendship for Allah. This might seem surprising given the Qur'anic mention of love, but the critical distinction is that friendship implies mutual need and similarity, which cannot apply to Allah. The proof is direct: if Allah is completely different from all contingents, then He cannot have a peer or friend that shares any attribute. Let's read the passage to see the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without footnotes to grasp the main claim. Then read the English translation to ensure understanding.
The passage is dense but concise.
2
Identify the definition of 'sadiq'
The passage defines 'sadiq' as a sincere companion truthful in affection. Understand this definition fully.
3
Understand the extension of the negation
Note that the negation applies to all types of close friends: near or far, affectionate or not, spouse or not. There is no exception.
4
Grasp the proof
The proof is that God is necessarily different from all contingent things (mukhalafa lil-hawadith). Since a friend would share some attribute or similarity, having a friend violates this necessary difference.
This proof is a corollary of God's absolute uniqueness.
5
Reflect on the implication
Reflect on why this does not contradict Qur'anic verses about God's love for believers. The key is that love is one-sided benevolence, not reciprocal friendship.
The footnote in the next lesson will clarify further.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) حَالَ كَونِه تعالى مُنَزَّها أيضًا عن الأصدقا) جمع صديق، بمعنى
و «المثل)) لأنَّ الحكم بنفي الشّبه يستلزم الحكم بنفي النَّظير والمثل ، فإنه إذا انتفى من يوافقه في أقل صفاته فَلَأَنْ ينتفي من يوافقه في أكثرها أو في جميعها من باب الأولى. محي.
المُصَادِق ؛ لصِدقه في وُدِّه ومحبته (۱) ، قريباً كان أو بعيدا، ملاطفا كان أو غيره (۲)، زوجاً كان أو لا، ودليل الجميع ما تقدم في وجوب مخالفته للحوادث .
(۱) وده... قوله: (لصدقه في وده ... الخ) إن قلت هذا المعنى ليس محالا وقد قال تعالى: وَيُحِبُّونَهُ ﴾ [المائدة: ٥٤] ﴿وَالَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا أَشَدُّ حُبًّا لِلَّهِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٦٥] ومنه الصديقون، قلت : المراد محالٌ على الوجه المُعتاد من أنَّ كُلاً يُعاون صاحبه وينفعه ويحتاج إليه. ومعنى يحبهم يفعل معهم ما يفعله المحبُّ مِن الإحسان ، ومن هذا المعنى: حبيب الله وخليل الله ، ولا يجوز أنْ يُطلق صديق الله ؛ لأنه لم يرد مع إيهامه المحال السابق، ولما ورَدَ الحبيب والخليل.. وجب قبوله وتأويله، وقد حكى شارحُ الدَّلائل خلافا في إضافة العشق له تعالى قياسا على المحبة، والأصح المنع ؛ لعدم الإذن مع إشعاره بالتعشق والتمازج. الأمير. (۲) قوله: (قريبا) :أي من غير واسطة . وقوله : ( بعيدا) أي: بواسطة أو وسائط . وقوله: (ملاطفا كان أو غيره أي سواء كان زائدا في المحبة والود أو لا، وإلا فالصادق في الود والمحبة لا يكون إلا ملاطفا. الشنواني.
(And) the state of Him, exalted, being also transcendent from (friends), plural of friend, meaning the sincere one in his affection and love (1), whether near or far, whether affectionate or otherwise (2), whether a spouse or not. And the proof of all is what preceded concerning the necessity of His being different from contingent things. (1) His affection... His saying: (due to his sincerity in his affection... etc.) If you say this meaning is not impossible and God has said 'they love Him' [Qur'an 5:54] and 'those who believe are more intense in love for God' [Qur'an 2:165], and among them are the friends, I say: what is meant is impossible in the customary manner that each aids his companion and benefits him and is in need of him. And the meaning of 'He loves them' is that He does with them what a lover does of goodness. And from this meaning are 'beloved of God' and 'friend of God', and it is not permissible to apply 'friend of God' (sadiq Allah) because it has not been reported with the implication of the previous impossibility. And when 'beloved' and 'friend' were reported, they must be accepted and interpreted. And the commentator of al-Dala'il has reported a disagreement regarding attributing passion ('ishq) to Him, exalted, by analogy with love. The more correct is prohibition because of lack of permission and because it suggests infatuation and intermingling. Al-Amir. (2) His saying: (near) means without intermediary. And his saying: (far) means through one or more intermediaries. And his saying: (affectionate or otherwise) means whether he is excessive in love and affection or not, otherwise the sincere one in affection and love is only affectionate. Al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage defines God's transcendence from having close friends (asdiqa'). It explains that the term 'friend' (sadiq) means a sincere companion in affection and love, whether near or far, affectionate or not, spouse or not. The proof for this transcendence is the same as the proof for God's being different from contingent beings. The footnote clarifies potential confusion: God's love for believers (reported in the Qur'an) is not the same as human friendship that entails mutual aid and need. The terms 'beloved' (habib) and 'friend' (khalil) are reported for certain prophets and are accepted, but the term 'friend' (sadiq) is not reported for God and would imply an inappropriate relationship. The footnote also discusses the meaning of 'near' and 'far' in the context of divine friendship.

صديق
أصدقاء
تنزيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God having close friends is possible because the Qur'an speaks of God's love for believers.
Correction: The passage clarifies that 'friend' in the human sense implies mutual need and similarity, which are impossible for God. God's love is one-sided benevolence, not reciprocal friendship.

Checkpoint
What is the proof that God has no close friends?
A) Because God is merciful
B) Because God is different from all contingent things
C) Because friends are only human
D) Because the Qur'an says so

Key Takeaway
God's absolute uniqueness and difference from all contingent beings precludes the possibility of any close friend.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that Allah has no close friends, how does that affect your relationship with Him? Are you ever tempted to treat Allah as a 'friend' who owes you something? How can you maintain love without slipping into an expectation of reciprocity?
?
The lesson says a friend implies mutual aid and need. In what ways do you subtly expect Allah to 'need' your worship? How can you purify your worship to be solely for His sake, not out of a sense of mutual benefit?
?
Consider your closest human friendships — they involve give-and-take. Now realize that Allah's relationship with you is not based on any need on His part. Does that make you feel small? How does that change your understanding of your own worth and your reliance on Him alone?

Clarifying the Terms of Divine Love: Why 'Sadiq' is Not Used
Footnote clarifying the objection about divine love and distinguishing terms like sadiq, habib, khalil, and ishq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nuanced distinction between permissible terms of divine love (habib, khalil) and the prohibited term sadiq, as well as the rejection of ishq.

Core Idea
Friendship implies need; God's love gives without needing.

The previous lesson established that God has no close friends. But what about the Qur'anic verses that speak of God's love for believers and the titles like 'friend of God' for prophets? This footnote addresses that very tension, explaining that the customary meaning of 'friend' involves reciprocity and need, which cannot apply to Allah. It also distinguishes the reported terms (habib, khalil) that are accepted with interpretation from the unreported term (sadiq) and the prohibited term (ishq).

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the answer
Read the passage which begins with 'If you say...' It presents an objection based on Qur'anic love, then the answer clarifies the difference.
2
Contrast human friendship with divine love
Note that human friendship involves mutual aid and need, whereas God's love is pure goodness without need.
3
Distinguish permissible terms
Realize that 'habib' (beloved) and 'khalil' (friend) are reported in revealed texts and are thus accepted, but they must be interpreted appropriately, unlike 'sadiq' which is not reported and implies need.
4
Understand the prohibition of 'ishq'
Note that 'ishq' (passionate love) is even more problematic because it suggests infatuation and intermingling, so it is prohibited by analogy.

The Rule of Tawqif for Allah's Names and Their Interpretation
Explains the rule that Allah's names require Scriptural authorization and how to interpret potentially deficient names.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle that Allah's names require Scriptural authorization and how names that appear to imply deficiency are interpreted in a way befitting Allah's transcendence.

Core Idea
Allah's names are not chosen by human opinion but by divine command.

This passage from al-Sanusi's Jawharat al-Tawhid establishes a fundamental rule: we cannot name Allah except as He has named Himself or as permitted by revelation. Moreover, some names like al-Sabur might seem to imply deficiency in their linguistic origin, so they must be interpreted in a way that upholds divine transcendence. Let's explore this principle and the method of interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of tawqif
Read the first part of the passage which states that applying names to Allah is restricted to permission from the Lawgiver. Note that this permission comes either through hearing the name in revelation or by the Lawgiver allowing its use.
The term 'tawqif' literally means 'stopping' or 'restriction' – we stop at what revelation says.
2
Distinguish between names that imply deficiency and those that imply praise
The passage explains that names which indicate praise are permissible by consensus, while those that might imply deficiency must be avoided or interpreted. Identify this distinction and the reasoning behind it.
The key is whether the name could give a wrong impression about Allah's perfection.
3
Examine the three examples: al-Sabur, al-Shakur, al-Halim
Read how each of these names is interpreted. Note the linguistic meaning that could imply deficiency and how the theologians reinterpret them in a way befitting Allah. For example, al-Sabur does not mean Allah experiences hardship but that He does not hasten punishment.
These examples illustrate the method of ta'wil (interpretation) that safeguards tanzih (divine transcendence).
4
Reflect on the underlying logic
Consider the analogy: if a human would not accept being called by a name not given by his parents, how much more does Allah deserve to be named only as He has named Himself. This reinforces the rule of tawqif.
The rule protects Allah's majesty and prevents anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان توقيف إطلاق أسماء الله وصفاته عَلى إذْنِ مِن الشَارع وإذْنِه في ذلك (۱) ، بأن يُسمَع مِن لسانه بطريق صحيح أو حَسَنٍ، أو يأذن في استعماله كذلك ؛ فما أَذنَ في إطلاقه واستعماله ممَّا لم يكن إطلاقه مُوهما نقصاً (۲) بل كان مُشعرًا بالمدح .. جازَ اتفاقا، وما لا ؛ فعلى المنع والتَّحريم (۳) ؛ إذْ لا يجوز أنْ يُسمَّى النَّبِيُّ الله بما ليس من أسمائه ، بل لو سُمِّيَ واحدٌ مِن أفرادِ النَّاس بما لم يُسمِّه به أبواه لما ارتضاه ، فالباري تعالى أولى ، وليس الكلام (٤) في أسمائه الأعلام الموضوعة في أسمائه الأعلام الموضوعة في اللغات(٥) ، وإِنَّما تأويله بمعنى لا يوهم: الصَّبور ، والشَّكور ، والحليم ، فإنَّ الصَّبور يوهم وصول مشقَّةٍ له تعالى بحسب أصل وضع اللغة ، لأنَّ الصَّبر عند أهل اللُّغة: حبسُ النَّفس على المشاق» لكنَّه يُطلق ويفسر بمعنى يليق به تعالى، فالصبور ـ على هذا ـ: هو الذي لا يُعجِّل بعقوبة من عصاه، والشكور يوهم وصول إحسان إليه من خلقه ، خلقه ، لأنَّ معنی الشكر لغة: الثَّناء على المُحسن، فيُفسر في حقه سبحانه يليق به، وهو: الذي يُجازي على قليل الطَّاعات بمعني الدرجات، ويُعطي بسبب العمل في الدنيا وهي أيام معدودة نعما في الآخرة غير محدودة، والحليم يوهم وصول أذى إليه تعالى، وهو سبحانه لا يصل إليه أذى، فيفسر الحليم في حقه : بالذي لا يُعجِّل بعقوبة من عصاه، فيرجع لمعنى الصَّبور، وهلم جرا. محي.
Explanation of the restriction (tawqif) of applying the names and attributes of Allah to the permission from the Legislator and His permission in that (1): that it be heard from his tongue by an authentic or good chain, or He permits its usage likewise. So what He permitted to apply and use, from what its application does not imply a deficiency (2) but rather indicates praise... it is permissible by consensus. And what not, then it is prohibited and forbidden (3); because it is not permissible to call the Prophet by what is not among his names; indeed, if a single individual among people were called by what his parents did not name him, he would not be pleased with it, so the Creator, exalted is He, is more worthy. And the discussion (4) is not about His proper names coined in languages (5), but rather its interpretation in a sense that does not imply: al-Sabur (the Patient), al-Shakur (the Thankful), and al-Halim (the Forbearing). For al-Sabur implies the arrival of hardship to Him, exalted is He, according to the original usage of the language, because al-sabr (patience) according to the people of language is restraining the soul from difficulties; but it is used and interpreted in a sense befitting Him, exalted is He. So al-Sabur, according to this, is the One who does not hasten to punish those who disobey Him. And al-Shakur implies the arrival of beneficence to Him from His creation, because the meaning of gratitude (shukr) in language is praising the benefactor; so it is interpreted in His regard, glorified is He, in a befitting manner, and He is the One who rewards for few acts of obedience with many degrees and gives through work in the worldly life, which are counted days, blessings in the Hereafter that are unlimited. And al-Halim implies the arrival of harm to Him, exalted is He, and He, glorified is He, is not reached by harm. So al-Halim is interpreted in His regard as the One who does not hasten to punish those who disobey Him, thus it returns to the meaning of al-Sabur, and so forth. Muhi.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage defines the rule of tawqif (restriction) for using names of Allah: that they must be based on Scriptural permission. It then explains how to handle names that might imply deficiency by ta'wil (interpretation) in a way befitting Allah. The passage begins by stating the condition: names are only allowed if heard from the Prophet or if the Lawgiver permits their use. Then it distinguishes between names that imply deficiency (which must be avoided or interpreted) and those that indicate praise (which are permissible by consensus). It emphasizes that Allah is more worthy than any human to be named only with what He has named Himself. The passage clarifies that the discussion is not about proper names like 'Allah' but about names derived from attributes such as al-Sabur, al-Shakur, al-Halim, which if taken literally suggest deficiency. Then it explains each: al-Sabur (Patient) might imply hardship for Allah, so it is interpreted as not hastening punishment; al-Shakur (Thankful) might imply receipt of beneficence, so it is interpreted as rewarding obedience generously; al-Halim (Forbearing) might imply harm reaching Allah, so it is interpreted similarly to al-Sabur. The passage thus shows how to uphold divine transcendence while using these names.

Key Terms
توقيف
سمعية
الصبور
الشكور
الحليم
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing that names like al-Sabur imply Allah experiences hardship or needs to be patient, or that al-Shakur means Allah benefits from His creation's gratitude.
Correction: The passage explains that such names must be interpreted in a way that befits Allah's perfection: al-Sabur means He does not hasten punishment, al-Shakur means He rewards abundantly, and al-Halim also means He does not hasten punishment.

Checkpoint
What is the rule regarding names of Allah that might imply a deficiency?
A) They are absolutely forbidden.
B) They are allowed but must be interpreted in a way befitting Allah.
C) They are allowed only if no alternative exists.
D) They can be used literally.

Key Takeaway
The use of Allah's names is restricted to revelation, and any name that might imply deficiency must be interpreted in a manner consistent with divine perfection.

The Sunni Approach to Ambiguous Texts: Tafwid and Ta'wil
Sanusi enumerates the two Sunni approaches to ambiguous texts and begins defining key terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two Sunni approaches (ta'wil and tafwid) to ambiguous scriptural texts about Allah's attributes and the importance of affirming transcendence.

Core Idea
Ambiguous texts about Allah are either interpreted or consigned — both affirm His transcendence.

Before delving into the details, Sanusi establishes the fundamental principle that any scriptural text that seems to imply resemblance between Allah and creation must be handled carefully. The People of the Sunnah have two valid methods: interpretation (ta'wil) or consignment (tafwid), both aimed at preserving Allah's transcendence. This lesson introduces these methods and the key terms needed to understand the debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the verse line that summarizes the two methods.
The passage begins with a heading declaring the Sunni way.
2
Identify the two methods
The verse line commands: 'interpret it or consign it' — these are ta'wil and tafwid. Understand that both aim at transcendence.
3
Note the key terms to be defined
Sanusi lists five terms: nass, tashbih, tafwid, al-Salaf, al-Khalaf. He will define them.
The passage only begins defining 'nass'.
4
Understand the definition of 'nass'
Nass here means scriptural evidence (Quran/Sunnah), as opposed to consensus, analogy, or deduction. It can be explicit or apparent.
This is the beginning of a longer definition.
5
Reflect on the principle
The key is to affirm Allah's transcendence (tanzih) over any literal anthropomorphism. Both methods preserve this.
This principle underlies all Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ بيانُ أنَّ مَسلكَ أهل السنّة في النُّصوص المُوهِمة هو التّفويضُ أو التَّأويلُ] ٤٠ - وكُلُّ نصَّ أَوهَمَ التَّشْبِيها أَولُهُ أَو فَوَّضْ وَرُمْ تَنْزِيهَا ولَمَّا قدَّمَ أَنَّه سبحانه وجبت مخالفته للحوادث عقلا وسمعا ، وَوَرَدَ في عبارة المصنّف في هذه المسألة ألفاظ يجب بيانها قبل الخوض في شرح هذا الموضوع؛ فيجب أولا بيان المراد من النَّصَّ ومن التَّشبيه ، والمراد مِن التّفويض، والمراد بالسلف والمراد بالخلف ، ثمَّ بيان ما اتَّفق عليه الفريقان، وما انفرد به أحدهما. أمَّا النَّصُّ ، فالمراد به في هذا الموضع ما قابل الإجماع والقياس والاستنباط ، وهو منحصر الدليل من الكتاب أو السُّنَّة ، سواء أكان صريحًا أم ظاهراً، وليس المراد ما قابل الظاهر.
[Statement that the way of the People of the Sunnah concerning texts that imply resemblance is consignment (tafwid) or interpretation (ta'wil)] 40 - And every text that implies resemblance, interpret it or consign it, and intend transcendence. And since he has presented that He, exalted, necessarily differs from contingent things by reason and revelation, and there occurred in the wording of the author in this issue words that must be explained before delving into the explanation of this topic; so first it is necessary to clarify the intended meaning of 'text' (nass) and of 'resemblance' (tashbih), and the intended meaning of 'consignment' (tafwid), and the intended meaning of 'the Salaf' and 'the Khalaf', then to clarify what the two groups agree upon and what each uniquely holds. As for 'text', what is meant by it in this context is what is opposed to consensus, analogy, and derivation, and it is confined to evidence from the Book or the Sunnah, whether it is explicit or apparent, and what is meant is not what is opposed to the apparent meaning.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage defines the Sunni methodology for dealing with ambiguous scriptural texts about Allah's attributes. It begins with the heading that the way of Ahl al-Sunnah is either tafwid (consigning the meaning to Allah) or ta'wil (interpretation). The verse line is then quoted: 'Every text that implies resemblance, interpret it or consign it, and intend transcendence.' The commentary then explains that since it has already been established that Allah is necessarily different from created things by both reason and revelation, the author (Laqani) uses certain terms that need clarification before proceeding. The commentary outlines what needs to be defined: 'nass' (text), 'tashbih' (resemblance), 'tafwid' (consignment), 'al-Salaf' (the early Muslims), and 'al-Khalaf' (the later Muslims). Then it explains the agreement and disagreement between the two groups. Specifically, it defines 'nass' here as that which is opposed to consensus, analogy, and deduction; it is limited to evidence from the Quran or Sunnah, whether explicit or apparent, and is not to be taken as meaning merely what is opposed to the apparent meaning. This passage establishes the fundamental principle that ambiguous texts must not be taken literally to imply anthropomorphism, but are to be either interpreted or consigned, always affirming Allah's transcendence.

Key Terms
النصوص الموهمة
التشبيه
التفويض
التأويل
السلف
الخلف
النص
التنزيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that tafwid means total ignorance of the meaning, leaving no understanding at all.
Correction: The Salaf consign the modality (kayfiyyah) while affirming the literal meaning in a way befitting Allah, as the verse commands to 'intend transcendence' — so they do have an understanding of the text's apparent meaning without anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint
According to the text, what are the two acceptable ways to handle a text that implies resemblance (tashbih)?
A) Rejection or allegory
B) Interpretation (ta'wil) or consignment (tafwid)
C) Literal acceptance or metaphorical interpretation
D) Abrogation or suspension

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunnah deal with ambiguous texts by either interpreting them in a way that befits Allah or consigning their true meaning to Allah, always affirming transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Sanusi insists that we must define our terms before debating. Which Qur'anic verses about Allah's attributes have you previously misunderstood because you lacked clear definitions? How will you safeguard yourself from falling into tashbih?

Method of Tafwid and Ta'wil: The Direction Example
Sanusi presents the method and applies it to the direction example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Salaf and Khalaf approach the verse implying direction for Allah, affirming transcendence while interpreting 'above-ness' differently.

Core Idea
Both Salaf and Khalaf deny direction for Allah, but differ in specifying the meaning of 'above'.

Sanusi introduces the two methods for handling problematic texts: tafwid (consigning the meaning to Allah) and ta'wil (interpreting figuratively). He then applies them to the verse 'They fear their Lord above them,' which seems to suggest Allah is in a direction. This lesson will clarify how each school upholds divine transcendence while dealing with the apparent implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problematic text
Read the passage to see which Quranic verse is presented as suggesting direction. Notice the phrase 'min fawqihim' (above them).
The verse is from Surah an-Nahl.
2
Compare Salaf and Khalaf interpretations
Note how both affirm transcendence but differ: Salaf affirm fawqiyya without knowing how, Khalaf interpret it as transcendence in glory.
3
Understand the method
This example illustrates the general method: for such texts, one either does tafwid (consign the meaning to Allah) or ta'wil (interpret metaphorically).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسلك في النصوص الموهمة هو التفويض أو التأويل
يوهم الجهة قوله تعالى: ﴿يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم مِّن فَوْقِهِمْ ﴾ [النحل: ٥٠] فالسلف يقولون: فمما تنزه الله تعالى عن أن يكون في جهة ، ونثبت له فوقيَّةٌ كما أثبتها لنفسه، ولكنها فوقية لا نعلم حقيقتها، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالفوقية معنى يليق به سبحانه ، وهو التعالي في فالمعنى: يخافُ الملائكةُ ربَّهم من أجل تعاليه في العظمة ومنه قوله تعالى: (الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ) [طه: ٥] فالسّلف يقولون: تُثبت له استواء كما أثبته لنفسه، ولكنَّه استواء لا نعلم حقيقته إلَّا بكونه لا يشبه استواء الحوادث المقتضي لما يقتضيه من الكون في جهة ، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالاستواء الاستيلاء والملك، وقد نُقل أنَّ رجلا سأل مالك بن أنس الإمامَ رضي الله تعالى عنه عن هذه الآية فَأَطْرَقَ مَليًّا ثمَّ قال: الاستواء غير مجهول، والكيف غير معقول، والإيمان به واجب ، والسُّؤال عنه بدعة ، وما أظنُّك إلا ضالا ، ثم أمر به فأخرج ويُروى أنَّ الزَّمخشري سأل الغزالي عن هذه الآية، فأجابه بقوله : إذا استحال أن تعرف نفسك بكيفيّة أو أَيْنيَّة فكيف يليق بعبوديتك أن تصفه تعالى بأين أو كيف وهو مُقدَّس عن ذلك ؟
ومما يوهم الجسمية قوله تعالى: ﴿وَجَاءَ رَبُّكَ ﴾ [الفجر: (۲۲] وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم فيما رواه البخاري ومسلم: (يَنْزِلُ رَبُّنا كل ليلة إلى سماء الدُّنيا حينَ يبقى ثلث الليل الأخير ، ويقولُ: مَن يدعوني فأستجيب له ؟ من يسألني فأعطيه ؟ مَنْ يَستغفِرُني فأغفر له ؟) فالسلف يقولون: مجيء ونزول لا نعلمهما ، والخلف يقولون : المراد بالآية : وجاء عذاب ربك، أو أمر ربك ، والمراد بما في الحديث : ينزل ملك ربك ، أو نحو ذلك . يوهم الصورة أنَّ أحمد والبخاري ومسلما رووا أنَّ رجلا ضرب عبده فنهاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال: «إنّ الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورته فالسَّلف يقولون : صورة لا نعلمها، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالصورة الصفة من سمع وبصر وحياة ; فهو على صفته في الجملة ، وإن كانت صفته تعالى قديمةً وصفة الإنسان حادثة ، وهذا كله مبني على أنّ الضمير في «صورته» عائد على الله تعالى، وهو ما تقتضيه رواية أخرى وردت في الحديث: «إن الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورة الرحمن ومن العلماء من جعل الضمير عائداً على الأخ المُصرَّح به في رواية مسلم بلفظ : «فإذا قاتل أحدكم أخاه فليجتنب الوجه ، فإن الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورته» أي : إذا كان كذلك فينبغي احترامه باتقاء الوجه، وقد روي أنه بلغ أحمد بن حنبل إمام
The method regarding problematic texts is tafwid or ta'wil. What suggests direction is His saying: 'They fear their Lord above them' [an-Nahl:50]. The Salaf say: We declare Allah transcendent from being in a direction, and we affirm for Him above-ness as He affirmed for Himself, but it is an above-ness whose reality we do not know. The Khalaf say: What is meant by above-ness is a meaning befitting Him, namely Transcendence in glory. So the meaning: The angels fear their Lord because of His transcendence in glory. And from that is His saying: 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' [Taha:5]. The Salaf say: We affirm Istawa as He affirmed for Himself, but it is an Istawa whose reality we do not know except that it does not resemble the istawa of contingent beings which requires what it entails of being in a direction. The Khalaf say: What is meant by istawa is domination and possession. It has been narrated that a man asked Imam Malik ibn Anas about this verse; he lowered his head for a long time, then said: 'Istawa is not unknown, the how is not comprehensible, belief in it is obligatory, asking about it is an innovation, and I think you are nothing but misguided.' Then he commanded that he be expelled. It is also narrated that al-Zamakhshari asked al-Ghazali about this verse, and he answered: 'If it is impossible for you to know yourself in terms of how or where, then how does it befit your servitude to describe Him, Exalted, with where or how, when He is sanctified above that?' What suggests corporeality is His saying: 'And your Lord comes' [al-Fajr:22] and His saying صلى الله عليه وسلم as narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'Our Lord descends every night to the lowest heaven when the last third of the night remains, and says: Who calls upon Me that I may respond to him? Who asks Me that I may give him? Who seeks forgiveness from Me that I may forgive him?' The Salaf say: Coming and descending we do not know them. The Khalaf say: What is meant by the verse is: the punishment of your Lord came, or the command of your Lord; and what is meant by the hadith is: the angel of your Lord descends, or similar. What suggests form is that Ahmad, al-Bukhari, and Muslim narrated that a man struck his slave; the Prophet forbade him and said: 'Indeed Allah created Adam upon His image.' The Salaf say: An image we do not know. The Khalaf say: What is meant by the image is the attribute of hearing, sight, and life; so he is upon His attribute in general, even though His attribute is eternal and man's attribute is temporally originated. All this is based on the pronoun in 'His image' referring to Allah, as required by another narration in the hadith: 'Indeed Allah created Adam upon the image of the Most Merciful.' Some scholars take the pronoun as referring to the brother mentioned in Muslim's narration: 'When one of you fights his brother, let him avoid the face, for indeed Allah created Adam upon his image,' i.e., if so, then it is fitting to respect him by avoiding the face. It has been narrated that this reached Ahmad ibn Hanbal, the Imam...
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage applies the methodologies of tafwid (Salaf) and ta'wil (Khalaf) to specific Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths that seem to imply direction, corporeality, or form for Allah. It takes each example in turn. First, the verse 'They fear their Lord above them' (an-Nahl:50) suggests direction (jihah). The Salaf say: We deny direction for Allah but affirm 'above-ness' (fawqiyyah) as He affirmed, without knowing its reality. The Khalaf interpret 'above-ness' as transcendence in glory (al-ta'ali fi al-'azamah), so the meaning is that angels fear their Lord's exaltedness. Second, the verse 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' (Taha:5). The Salaf affirm istiwa' without knowing its how, denying similarity to creation's istiwa'. The Khalaf interpret it as domination (istila) and possession (mulk). The passage then quotes Imam Malik's response to the questioner: istiwa is not unknown, the modality is incomprehensible, belief is obligatory, asking is an innovation. It also quotes al-Ghazali's response to al-Zamakhshari: if you cannot know your own how or where, how can you ask about Allah's? Third, the verse 'And your Lord comes' (al-Fajr:22) and the hadith of descent. Salaf: we do not know the reality of coming and descending. Khalaf: the verse means His punishment or command came; the hadith means an angel descends. Fourth, the hadith about Adam created upon Allah's image. Salaf: we do not know the image. Khalaf: 'image' means attributes like hearing, sight, life; man is upon Allah's attributes in a general sense, though Allah's attributes are eternal and man's are temporal. The passage notes that the pronoun may refer to Allah or to the person being struck, citing alternate narrations. It concludes by mentioning that this reached Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal (the text cuts off).

Key Terms
التفويض
التأويل
الفوقية
الجهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) They interpret 'above' as transcendence in glory.
C) They reject the verse as unreliable.
D) They say the verse refers to the angels' own above-ness.

Key Takeaway
Both Salaf and Khalaf agree that Allah is not in a direction, but they differ on how to understand the word 'above' in the verse.

The Throne Verse: Istiwa According to Salaf and Khalaf
Sanusi presents the istiwa example with Salaf and Khalaf views, then quotes Malik and Ghazali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Salaf and Khalaf approaches to the verse 'al-Rahman 'ala al-'arsh istawa,' including the famous responses of Imam Malik and al-Ghazali.

Core Idea
Istiwa is affirmed but not like creation; the Salaf consign its reality, the Khalaf interpret it as domination.

The verse 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' is one of the most debated anthropomorphic texts. Sanusi presents the Salaf and Khalaf positions, then quotes Imam Malik's famous response and al-Ghazali's answer to al-Zamakhshari. This lesson will help you grasp the key points and the method of tafwid and ta'wil in action.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and positions
Read the verse 'al-Rahman 'ala al-'arsh istawa' and note the Salaf and Khalaf interpretations as presented.
The Salaf say istiwa is known in meaning but unknown in how; Khalaf say it means domination.
2
Examine Malik's response
Read the anecdote of the man asking Imam Malik. Understand the key phrases: 'istiwa is not unknown, the how is not comprehensible, belief is obligatory, asking is an innovation.'
Malik emphasizes that the meaning is known but the modality is beyond reason.
3
Examine Ghazali's response
Read al-Ghazali's reply to al-Zamakhshari. Note how he uses the analogy of self-knowledge to argue that we cannot ask 'how' or 'where' about Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسلك في النصوص الموهمة هو التفويض أو التأويل
يوهم الجهة قوله تعالى: ﴿يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم مِّن فَوْقِهِمْ ﴾ [النحل: ٥٠] فالسلف يقولون: فمما تنزه الله تعالى عن أن يكون في جهة ، ونثبت له فوقيَّةٌ كما أثبتها لنفسه، ولكنها فوقية لا نعلم حقيقتها، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالفوقية معنى يليق به سبحانه ، وهو التعالي في فالمعنى: يخافُ الملائكةُ ربَّهم من أجل تعاليه في العظمة ومنه قوله تعالى: (الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ) [طه: ٥] فالسّلف يقولون: تُثبت له استواء كما أثبته لنفسه، ولكنَّه استواء لا نعلم حقيقته إلَّا بكونه لا يشبه استواء الحوادث المقتضي لما يقتضيه من الكون في جهة ، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالاستواء الاستيلاء والملك، وقد نُقل أنَّ رجلا سأل مالك بن أنس الإمامَ رضي الله تعالى عنه عن هذه الآية فَأَطْرَقَ مَليًّا ثمَّ قال: الاستواء غير مجهول، والكيف غير معقول، والإيمان به واجب ، والسُّؤال عنه بدعة ، وما أظنُّك إلا ضالا ، ثم أمر به فأخرج ويُروى أنَّ الزَّمخشري سأل الغزالي عن هذه الآية، فأجابه بقوله : إذا استحال أن تعرف نفسك بكيفيّة أو أَيْنيَّة فكيف يليق بعبوديتك أن تصفه تعالى بأين أو كيف وهو مُقدَّس عن ذلك ؟
ومما يوهم الجسمية قوله تعالى: ﴿وَجَاءَ رَبُّكَ ﴾ [الفجر: (۲۲] وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم فيما رواه البخاري ومسلم: (يَنْزِلُ رَبُّنا كل ليلة إلى سماء الدُّنيا حينَ يبقى ثلث الليل الأخير ، ويقولُ: مَن يدعوني فأستجيب له ؟ من يسألني فأعطيه ؟ مَنْ يَستغفِرُني فأغفر له ؟) فالسلف يقولون: مجيء ونزول لا نعلمهما ، والخلف يقولون : المراد بالآية : وجاء عذاب ربك، أو أمر ربك ، والمراد بما في الحديث : ينزل ملك ربك ، أو نحو ذلك . يوهم الصورة أنَّ أحمد والبخاري ومسلما رووا أنَّ رجلا ضرب عبده فنهاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال: «إنّ الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورته فالسَّلف يقولون : صورة لا نعلمها، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالصورة الصفة من سمع وبصر وحياة ; فهو على صفته في الجملة ، وإن كانت صفته تعالى قديمةً وصفة الإنسان حادثة ، وهذا كله مبني على أنّ الضمير في «صورته» عائد على الله تعالى، وهو ما تقتضيه رواية أخرى وردت في الحديث: «إن الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورة الرحمن ومن العلماء من جعل الضمير عائداً على الأخ المُصرَّح به في رواية مسلم بلفظ : «فإذا قاتل أحدكم أخاه فليجتنب الوجه ، فإن الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورته» أي : إذا كان كذلك فينبغي احترامه باتقاء الوجه، وقد روي أنه بلغ أحمد بن حنبل إمام
The method regarding problematic texts is tafwid or ta'wil. What suggests direction is His saying: 'They fear their Lord above them' [an-Nahl:50]. The Salaf say: We declare Allah transcendent from being in a direction, and we affirm for Him above-ness as He affirmed for Himself, but it is an above-ness whose reality we do not know. The Khalaf say: What is meant by above-ness is a meaning befitting Him, namely Transcendence in glory. So the meaning: The angels fear their Lord because of His transcendence in glory. And from that is His saying: 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' [Taha:5]. The Salaf say: We affirm Istawa as He affirmed for Himself, but it is an Istawa whose reality we do not know except that it does not resemble the istawa of contingent beings which requires what it entails of being in a direction. The Khalaf say: What is meant by istawa is domination and possession. It has been narrated that a man asked Imam Malik ibn Anas about this verse; he lowered his head for a long time, then said: 'Istawa is not unknown, the how is not comprehensible, belief in it is obligatory, asking about it is an innovation, and I think you are nothing but misguided.' Then he commanded that he be expelled. It is also narrated that al-Zamakhshari asked al-Ghazali about this verse, and he answered: 'If it is impossible for you to know yourself in terms of how or where, then how does it befit your servitude to describe Him, Exalted, with where or how, when He is sanctified above that?' What suggests corporeality is His saying: 'And your Lord comes' [al-Fajr:22] and His saying صلى الله عليه وسلم as narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'Our Lord descends every night to the lowest heaven when the last third of the night remains, and says: Who calls upon Me that I may respond to him? Who asks Me that I may give him? Who seeks forgiveness from Me that I may forgive him?' The Salaf say: Coming and descending we do not know them. The Khalaf say: What is meant by the verse is: the punishment of your Lord came, or the command of your Lord; and what is meant by the hadith is: the angel of your Lord descends, or similar. What suggests form is that Ahmad, al-Bukhari, and Muslim narrated that a man struck his slave; the Prophet forbade him and said: 'Indeed Allah created Adam upon His image.' The Salaf say: An image we do not know. The Khalaf say: What is meant by the image is the attribute of hearing, sight, and life; so he is upon His attribute in general, even though His attribute is eternal and man's attribute is temporally originated. All this is based on the pronoun in 'His image' referring to Allah, as required by another narration in the hadith: 'Indeed Allah created Adam upon the image of the Most Merciful.' Some scholars take the pronoun as referring to the brother mentioned in Muslim's narration: 'When one of you fights his brother, let him avoid the face, for indeed Allah created Adam upon his image,' i.e., if so, then it is fitting to respect him by avoiding the face. It has been narrated that this reached Ahmad ibn Hanbal, the Imam...
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage applies the methodologies of tafwid (Salaf) and ta'wil (Khalaf) to specific Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths that seem to imply direction, corporeality, or form for Allah. It takes each example in turn. First, the verse 'They fear their Lord above them' (an-Nahl:50) suggests direction (jihah). The Salaf say: We deny direction for Allah but affirm 'above-ness' (fawqiyyah) as He affirmed, without knowing its reality. The Khalaf interpret 'above-ness' as transcendence in glory (al-ta'ali fi al-'azamah), so the meaning is that angels fear their Lord's exaltedness. Second, the verse 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' (Taha:5). The Salaf affirm istiwa' without knowing its how, denying similarity to creation's istiwa'. The Khalaf interpret it as domination (istila) and possession (mulk). The passage then quotes Imam Malik's response to the questioner: istiwa is not unknown, the modality is incomprehensible, belief is obligatory, asking is an innovation. It also quotes al-Ghazali's response to al-Zamakhshari: if you cannot know your own how or where, how can you ask about Allah's? Third, the verse 'And your Lord comes' (al-Fajr:22) and the hadith of descent. Salaf: we do not know the reality of coming and descending. Khalaf: the verse means His punishment or command came; the hadith means an angel descends. Fourth, the hadith about Adam created upon Allah's image. Salaf: we do not know the image. Khalaf: 'image' means attributes like hearing, sight, life; man is upon Allah's attributes in a general sense, though Allah's attributes are eternal and man's are temporal. The passage notes that the pronoun may refer to Allah or to the person being struck, citing alternate narrations. It concludes by mentioning that this reached Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal (the text cuts off).

Key Terms
الاستواء
الاستيلاء
الملك
الكيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Imam Malik say about istiwa?
A) It is completely unknown.
B) It is known but the modality is incomprehensible.
C) It means domination.
D) It is a metaphor for creation.

Key Takeaway
The Salaf avoid specifying the meaning of istiwa, while the Khalaf interpret it as dominion, and both emphasize Allah's transcendence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'الرحمن على العرش استوى', do you feel an urge to visualize God sitting? How can you train your heart to be content with 'بلا كيف' (without how) in your worship?
?
If someone pressed you to explain exactly how Allah is above His Throne, would your reaction be closer to Malik's stern dismissal or to providing a philosophical answer? What does that reveal about your trust in Allah's transcendence?
?
How does the realization that you cannot fully know even your own soul (as al-Ghazali pointed out) humble your approach to knowing Allah? Will you now surrender more to the revealed texts without demanding explanations?

Divine Transcendence
intermediate
5 min
Texts of Coming and Descending: Salaf and Khalaf Perspectives
Sanusi applies tafwid and ta'wil to the coming and descending texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Salaf and Khalaf interpret the verse about Allah's 'coming' and the hadith of 'descending' without attributing movement to Allah.

Core Idea
Coming and descending are affirmed without modality by Salaf, interpreted as punishment or angel by Khalaf.

Sanusi addresses two texts that might imply Allah moves or changes: the verse 'And your Lord comes' and the hadith of nightly descent. Both schools deny literal movement, but differ in interpretation. This lesson examines their approaches.

Guided Path
1
Read the problematic texts
Read the verse 'And your Lord comes' and the hadith about Allah's descent. Notice the potential implication of movement.
The verse is from al-Fajr, the hadith is from Bukhari and Muslim.
2
Understand the Salaf position
The Salaf say: 'Coming and descending we do not know them.' They affirm the words without specifying how, consigning the reality to Allah.
3
Understand the Khalaf position
The Khalaf interpret: 'the verse means the punishment of your Lord came, or His command; the hadith means an angel descends.' They provide a non-literal meaning.

According to the Khalaf, what is the interpretation of the verse 'And your Lord comes'?
A) Allah physically comes.
B) The meaning is unknown.
C) The punishment or command of your Lord came.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'And your Lord comes,' do you feel the urgency of standing before Him on that Day? How does your understanding of this text—whether through tafwid or ta'wil—affect your heart's preparation for that moment?
?
The Prophet told us that Allah descends every last third of the night. Have you ever truly responded to His call in those hours? What keeps you from seeking Him in that time, knowing He invites you personally?

The Hadith of Adam's Creation: Salaf and Khalaf on 'Image'
Sanusi applies tafwid and ta'wil to the form-implicating hadith and discusses the pronoun reference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Salaf and Khalaf interpretations of the hadith 'Allah created Adam upon His image' and the issue of the pronoun reference.

Core Idea
Both schools deny that Allah has a physical image; the difference is in interpreting 'image' as unknown attribute or as human attributes.

The hadith about Adam being created upon Allah's image can suggest anthropomorphism. Sanusi presents the Salaf approach (affirming the image without knowing its reality) and the Khalaf approach (interpreting image as attributes). He also discusses the pronoun reference controversy. This lesson clarifies these nuanced positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and Salaf view
Read the hadith as narrated by Ahmad, Bukhari, and Muslim. Note the Salaf response: 'An image we do not know.'
The hadith is about a man striking his slave.
2
Understand the Khalaf view
The Khalaf interpret 'image' as the attributes of hearing, sight, and life. Man is upon Allah's attributes in a general sense, though Allah's attributes are eternal and man's are temporal.
3
Consider the pronoun reference debate
Some scholars say the pronoun in 'His image' refers to Allah; others say it refers to the brother being struck. This affects the meaning.
The alternate narration says 'upon the image of the Most Merciful.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسلك في النصوص الموهمة هو التفويض أو التأويل
يوهم الجهة قوله تعالى: ﴿يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم مِّن فَوْقِهِمْ ﴾ [النحل: ٥٠] فالسلف يقولون: فمما تنزه الله تعالى عن أن يكون في جهة ، ونثبت له فوقيَّةٌ كما أثبتها لنفسه، ولكنها فوقية لا نعلم حقيقتها، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالفوقية معنى يليق به سبحانه ، وهو التعالي في فالمعنى: يخافُ الملائكةُ ربَّهم من أجل تعاليه في العظمة ومنه قوله تعالى: (الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ) [طه: ٥] فالسّلف يقولون: تُثبت له استواء كما أثبته لنفسه، ولكنَّه استواء لا نعلم حقيقته إلَّا بكونه لا يشبه استواء الحوادث المقتضي لما يقتضيه من الكون في جهة ، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالاستواء الاستيلاء والملك، وقد نُقل أنَّ رجلا سأل مالك بن أنس الإمامَ رضي الله تعالى عنه عن هذه الآية فَأَطْرَقَ مَليًّا ثمَّ قال: الاستواء غير مجهول، والكيف غير معقول، والإيمان به واجب ، والسُّؤال عنه بدعة ، وما أظنُّك إلا ضالا ، ثم أمر به فأخرج ويُروى أنَّ الزَّمخشري سأل الغزالي عن هذه الآية، فأجابه بقوله : إذا استحال أن تعرف نفسك بكيفيّة أو أَيْنيَّة فكيف يليق بعبوديتك أن تصفه تعالى بأين أو كيف وهو مُقدَّس عن ذلك ؟
ومما يوهم الجسمية قوله تعالى: ﴿وَجَاءَ رَبُّكَ ﴾ [الفجر: (۲۲] وقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم فيما رواه البخاري ومسلم: (يَنْزِلُ رَبُّنا كل ليلة إلى سماء الدُّنيا حينَ يبقى ثلث الليل الأخير ، ويقولُ: مَن يدعوني فأستجيب له ؟ من يسألني فأعطيه ؟ مَنْ يَستغفِرُني فأغفر له ؟) فالسلف يقولون: مجيء ونزول لا نعلمهما ، والخلف يقولون : المراد بالآية : وجاء عذاب ربك، أو أمر ربك ، والمراد بما في الحديث : ينزل ملك ربك ، أو نحو ذلك . يوهم الصورة أنَّ أحمد والبخاري ومسلما رووا أنَّ رجلا ضرب عبده فنهاه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال: «إنّ الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورته فالسَّلف يقولون : صورة لا نعلمها، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالصورة الصفة من سمع وبصر وحياة ; فهو على صفته في الجملة ، وإن كانت صفته تعالى قديمةً وصفة الإنسان حادثة ، وهذا كله مبني على أنّ الضمير في «صورته» عائد على الله تعالى، وهو ما تقتضيه رواية أخرى وردت في الحديث: «إن الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورة الرحمن ومن العلماء من جعل الضمير عائداً على الأخ المُصرَّح به في رواية مسلم بلفظ : «فإذا قاتل أحدكم أخاه فليجتنب الوجه ، فإن الله تعالى خلق آدم على صورته» أي : إذا كان كذلك فينبغي احترامه باتقاء الوجه، وقد روي أنه بلغ أحمد بن حنبل إمام
The method regarding problematic texts is tafwid or ta'wil. What suggests direction is His saying: 'They fear their Lord above them' [an-Nahl:50]. The Salaf say: We declare Allah transcendent from being in a direction, and we affirm for Him above-ness as He affirmed for Himself, but it is an above-ness whose reality we do not know. The Khalaf say: What is meant by above-ness is a meaning befitting Him, namely Transcendence in glory. So the meaning: The angels fear their Lord because of His transcendence in glory. And from that is His saying: 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' [Taha:5]. The Salaf say: We affirm Istawa as He affirmed for Himself, but it is an Istawa whose reality we do not know except that it does not resemble the istawa of contingent beings which requires what it entails of being in a direction. The Khalaf say: What is meant by istawa is domination and possession. It has been narrated that a man asked Imam Malik ibn Anas about this verse; he lowered his head for a long time, then said: 'Istawa is not unknown, the how is not comprehensible, belief in it is obligatory, asking about it is an innovation, and I think you are nothing but misguided.' Then he commanded that he be expelled. It is also narrated that al-Zamakhshari asked al-Ghazali about this verse, and he answered: 'If it is impossible for you to know yourself in terms of how or where, then how does it befit your servitude to describe Him, Exalted, with where or how, when He is sanctified above that?' What suggests corporeality is His saying: 'And your Lord comes' [al-Fajr:22] and His saying صلى الله عليه وسلم as narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'Our Lord descends every night to the lowest heaven when the last third of the night remains, and says: Who calls upon Me that I may respond to him? Who asks Me that I may give him? Who seeks forgiveness from Me that I may forgive him?' The Salaf say: Coming and descending we do not know them. The Khalaf say: What is meant by the verse is: the punishment of your Lord came, or the command of your Lord; and what is meant by the hadith is: the angel of your Lord descends, or similar. What suggests form is that Ahmad, al-Bukhari, and Muslim narrated that a man struck his slave; the Prophet forbade him and said: 'Indeed Allah created Adam upon His image.' The Salaf say: An image we do not know. The Khalaf say: What is meant by the image is the attribute of hearing, sight, and life; so he is upon His attribute in general, even though His attribute is eternal and man's attribute is temporally originated. All this is based on the pronoun in 'His image' referring to Allah, as required by another narration in the hadith: 'Indeed Allah created Adam upon the image of the Most Merciful.' Some scholars take the pronoun as referring to the brother mentioned in Muslim's narration: 'When one of you fights his brother, let him avoid the face, for indeed Allah created Adam upon his image,' i.e., if so, then it is fitting to respect him by avoiding the face. It has been narrated that this reached Ahmad ibn Hanbal, the Imam...
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage applies the methodologies of tafwid (Salaf) and ta'wil (Khalaf) to specific Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths that seem to imply direction, corporeality, or form for Allah. It takes each example in turn. First, the verse 'They fear their Lord above them' (an-Nahl:50) suggests direction (jihah). The Salaf say: We deny direction for Allah but affirm 'above-ness' (fawqiyyah) as He affirmed, without knowing its reality. The Khalaf interpret 'above-ness' as transcendence in glory (al-ta'ali fi al-'azamah), so the meaning is that angels fear their Lord's exaltedness. Second, the verse 'The Most Merciful established Himself over the Throne' (Taha:5). The Salaf affirm istiwa' without knowing its how, denying similarity to creation's istiwa'. The Khalaf interpret it as domination (istila) and possession (mulk). The passage then quotes Imam Malik's response to the questioner: istiwa is not unknown, the modality is incomprehensible, belief is obligatory, asking is an innovation. It also quotes al-Ghazali's response to al-Zamakhshari: if you cannot know your own how or where, how can you ask about Allah's? Third, the verse 'And your Lord comes' (al-Fajr:22) and the hadith of descent. Salaf: we do not know the reality of coming and descending. Khalaf: the verse means His punishment or command came; the hadith means an angel descends. Fourth, the hadith about Adam created upon Allah's image. Salaf: we do not know the image. Khalaf: 'image' means attributes like hearing, sight, life; man is upon Allah's attributes in a general sense, though Allah's attributes are eternal and man's are temporal. The passage notes that the pronoun may refer to Allah or to the person being struck, citing alternate narrations. It concludes by mentioning that this reached Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal (the text cuts off).

Key Terms
الصورة
الصفة
الرحمن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Khalaf interpretation of 'image' in the hadith?
A) It is a physical form.
B) It refers to attributes such as hearing and sight.
C) It is unknown.
D) It means the face.

Key Takeaway
The hadith does not imply that Allah has a physical form; Salaf consign the meaning, Khalaf interpret it as attributes, and the pronoun reference is debated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a hadith that seems to describe Allah in human-like terms, do you find yourself immediately wanting to interpret it to make it more 'understandable', or can you embrace the Salaf's stance of 'we do not know' and trust Allah's wisdom? What does your reaction reveal about your reliance on divine revelation versus human reason?
?
The hadith also teaches that striking the face is forbidden because Allah created Adam upon his image. Think of a time you insulted or harmed someone's dignity, perhaps without physical violence. Did you consider that you were disrespecting something that carries a divine imprint? How can you change your attitude toward others in light of this?
?
The pronoun debate shows that even the interpretation of a single word can have profound theological and ethical implications. Are you willing to invest the effort to understand the deeper dimensions of sacred texts, or do you settle for surface-level readings? What would it cost you to dive deeper?

The Two Methods: Tafwīḍ and Ta'wīl with the Example of Jiha
The author defines the two methods and gives the example of jiha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two methods (tafwīḍ and ta'wīl) for dealing with ambiguous Qur'anic texts and how they are applied to the concept of divine direction (jiha).

Core Idea
When texts seem to describe Allah in human terms, scholars either consign the meaning or interpret it figuratively.

This lesson introduces two fundamental ways Muslim scholars have approached Qur'anic verses that appear to attribute spatial or physical qualities to Allah. The author first defines the two methods—tafwīḍ and ta'wīl—and then applies them to the verse about 'above' (fawqiyya). Understanding these methods is essential for preserving divine transcendence (tanzih) while affirming what Allah has said about Himself.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify the two methods
Read the passage carefully and note the two methods: tafwīḍ and ta'wīl.
The passage begins with a clear statement of the two methods.
2
Observe the verse suggesting direction
The verse 'They fear their Lord from above them' seems to imply Allah is in a direction. How do the salaf and khalaf respond?
3
Compare salaf and khalaf positions
Both affirm Allah's transcendence, but differ in approach: salaf consign modality, khalaf interpret metaphorically.
Tafwīḍ does not mean denial; it is affirmative consignment.
4
Reflect on the significance
Why does the author present both views? How do they both preserve tanzih?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسلك في النصوص الموهمة هو التفويض أو التأويل
يوهم الجهة قوله تعالى: ﴿يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم مِّن فَوْقِهِمْ ﴾ [النحل: ٥٠] فالسلف يقولون: فمما تنزه الله تعالى عن أن يكون في جهة ، ونثبت له فوقيَّةٌ كما أثبتها لنفسه، ولكنها فوقية لا نعلم حقيقتها، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالفوقية معنى يليق به سبحانه ، وهو التعالي في فالمعنى: يخافُ الملائكةُ ربَّهم من أجل تعاليه في العظمة ومنه قوله تعالى: (الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ) [طه: ٥] فالسّلف يقولون: تُثبت له استواء كما أثبته لنفسه، ولكنَّه استواء لا نعلم حقيقته إلَّا بكونه لا يشبه استواء الحوادث المقتضي لما يقتضيه من الكون في جهة ، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالاستواء الاستيلاء والملك، وقد نُقل أنَّ رجلا سأل مالك بن أنس الإمامَ رضي الله تعالى عنه عن هذه الآية فَأَطْرَقَ مَليًّا ثمَّ قال: الاستواء غير مجهول، والكيف غير معقول، والإيمان به واجب ، والسُّؤال عنه بدعة ، وما أظنُّك إلا ضالا ، ثم أمر به فأخرج ويُروى أنَّ الزَّمخشري سأل الغزالي عن هذه الآية، فأجابه بقوله : إذا استحال أن تعرف نفسك بكيفيّة أو أَيْنيَّة فكيف يليق بعبوديتك أن تصفه تعالى بأين أو كيف وهو مُقدَّس عن ذلك ؟
The method regarding texts that suggest [anthropomorphism] is consignment (tafwīḍ) or interpretation (ta’wīl). The verse 'They fear their Lord from above them' (16:50) suggests direction. The salaf say: We transcend Allah from being in a direction, and we affirm for Him 'above-ness' (fawqiyya) as He affirmed for Himself, but it is an above-ness whose reality we do not know. The khalaf say: What is meant by above-ness is a meaning befitting Him, which is exaltedness in majesty. So the meaning is: The angels fear their Lord because of His exaltedness in majesty. And from it is His saying: 'The Most Merciful rose over the Throne' (20:5). The salaf say: We affirm for Him a rising (istiwa') as He affirmed for Himself, but it is a rising whose reality we do not know except that it does not resemble the rising of created things which necessitates what it necessitates of being in a direction. The khalaf say: What is meant by rising is conquest and dominion. It is reported that a man asked Imam Malik ibn Anas, may Allah be pleased with him, about this verse, and he lowered his head for a long time, then said: 'The rising is not unknown, the modality is not comprehensible, belief in it is obligatory, questioning about it is an innovation, and I think you are nothing but misguided.' Then he ordered him to be taken out. And it is narrated that al-Zamakhshari asked al-Ghazali about this verse, and he answered him by saying: 'Since it is impossible for you to know yourself by a modality (kayfiyya) or a location (ayniyya), how is it fitting for your servitude that you describe Him, exalted, by a 'where' or a 'how', while He is sanctified above that?'
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the two methods for dealing with ambiguous texts (nusus muwhima) that seem to imply anthropomorphism: tafwīḍ (consigning the meaning to Allah without specifying) and ta'wīl (interpretation in a way befitting Allah). The author then gives the first example: the verse 'They fear their Lord from above them' which seems to imply Allah is in a direction (jiha). He explains the salaf position: they negate any literal direction for Allah, but affirm the attribute of 'above-ness' as Allah affirmed it for Himself, while admitting ignorance of its reality. The khalaf interpret 'above' as meaning 'exalted in majesty'. Next, the author discusses the verse of istiwa' (rising over the Throne). Again, the salaf affirm it without knowing how, emphasizing it does not resemble created rising. The khalaf interpret it as 'istila'' (conquest) or 'mulk' (dominion). The author then quotes Imam Malik's famous response to a question about istiwa': he declared that the reality of istiwa' is known, its modality is inconceivable, belief in it is obligatory, and asking about it is an innovation. Finally, he relates the anecdote of al-Zamakhshari asking al-Ghazali about the same verse; al-Ghazali's reply uses a logical analogy: if you cannot understand your own self in terms of 'how' or 'where', how can you ask such questions about Allah?

Key Terms
تفويض
تأويل
الجهة
الفوقية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think tafwīḍ means denying the attribute entirely.
Correction: Tafwīḍ actually affirms the attribute while consigning its reality and modality to Allah, as the salaf did with fawqiyya.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the salaf affirm regarding the verse 'يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم مِّن فَوْقِهِمْ'?
A) They deny any meaning of 'above'.
B) They affirm above-ness without knowing its reality.
C) They interpret above as exaltedness.
D) They say it applies only to angels.

Key Takeaway
The two methods—tafwīḍ and ta'wīl—both safeguard Allah's transcendence, with the former affirming the attribute without modality and the latter interpreting it in a befitting manner.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'They fear their Lord from above them', do you feel comfortable not knowing how Allah is 'above'? Or does your mind immediately try to interpret it in a way that makes logical sense? What does that tell you about your trust in revelation versus your own intellect?
?
The salaf were content to say 'we do not know the reality of fawqiyya'. Could you sincerely say that about every ambiguous attribute? Which attribute would be the hardest for you to consign without explanation?
?
Imagine you're teaching someone about Allah's transcendence. Would you lean towards explaining tafwīḍ or ta'wīl? Why? Does your preference reflect a desire to protect Allah's majesty or to satisfy your own need for clarity?

The Example of Istiwa' and the Responses of Imam Malik and al-Ghazali
The author discusses the verse of istiwa' and reports two scholarly responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the salaf and khalaf positions on the verse of istiwa' and the key arguments made by Imam Malik and al-Ghazali against questioning its modality.

Core Idea
The verse 'الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى' is a classic test case for how both methods handle divine attributes.

This lesson continues from the previous one, now applying the two methods to the famous verse about Allah's 'rising' over the Throne. After presenting the salaf and khalaf interpretations, the author reports two key incidents: Imam Malik's stern rebuke of a questioner and al-Ghazali's logical analogy. These responses illustrate the proper attitude of reverent acceptance or reasoned interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on istiwa'
Read the full Arabic passage and translation. Note the salaf and khalaf positions on istiwa'.
The salaf affirm without modality; the khalaf interpret as dominion.
2
Analyze Imam Malik's response
Malik's statement: 'the rising is not unknown, the modality is not comprehensible, belief is obligatory, questioning is innovation.' What does this imply?
Malik forbids asking 'how' (kayf).
3
Analyze al-Ghazali's analogy
Al-Ghazali compares knowing Allah to knowing oneself: if you cannot know yourself by 'how' or 'where', how can you ask that about Allah?
This highlights the limits of human reason.
4
Synthesize the two methods
How do these anecdotes reinforce the two methods? Do they favor one over the other?

المسلك في النصوص الموهمة هو التفويض أو التأويل
يوهم الجهة قوله تعالى: ﴿يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم مِّن فَوْقِهِمْ ﴾ [النحل: ٥٠] فالسلف يقولون: فمما تنزه الله تعالى عن أن يكون في جهة ، ونثبت له فوقيَّةٌ كما أثبتها لنفسه، ولكنها فوقية لا نعلم حقيقتها، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالفوقية معنى يليق به سبحانه ، وهو التعالي في فالمعنى: يخافُ الملائكةُ ربَّهم من أجل تعاليه في العظمة ومنه قوله تعالى: (الرَّحْمَنُ عَلَى الْعَرْشِ اسْتَوَى ) [طه: ٥] فالسّلف يقولون: تُثبت له استواء كما أثبته لنفسه، ولكنَّه استواء لا نعلم حقيقته إلَّا بكونه لا يشبه استواء الحوادث المقتضي لما يقتضيه من الكون في جهة ، والخلف يقولون: المراد بالاستواء الاستيلاء والملك، وقد نُقل أنَّ رجلا سأل مالك بن أنس الإمامَ رضي الله تعالى عنه عن هذه الآية فَأَطْرَقَ مَليًّا ثمَّ قال: الاستواء غير مجهول، والكيف غير معقول، والإيمان به واجب ، والسُّؤال عنه بدعة ، وما أظنُّك إلا ضالا ، ثم أمر به فأخرج ويُروى أنَّ الزَّمخشري سأل الغزالي عن هذه الآية، فأجابه بقوله : إذا استحال أن تعرف نفسك بكيفيّة أو أَيْنيَّة فكيف يليق بعبوديتك أن تصفه تعالى بأين أو كيف وهو مُقدَّس عن ذلك ؟
The method regarding texts that suggest [anthropomorphism] is consignment (tafwīḍ) or interpretation (ta’wīl). The verse 'They fear their Lord from above them' (16:50) suggests direction. The salaf say: We transcend Allah from being in a direction, and we affirm for Him 'above-ness' (fawqiyya) as He affirmed for Himself, but it is an above-ness whose reality we do not know. The khalaf say: What is meant by above-ness is a meaning befitting Him, which is exaltedness in majesty. So the meaning is: The angels fear their Lord because of His exaltedness in majesty. And from it is His saying: 'The Most Merciful rose over the Throne' (20:5). The salaf say: We affirm for Him a rising (istiwa') as He affirmed for Himself, but it is a rising whose reality we do not know except that it does not resemble the rising of created things which necessitates what it necessitates of being in a direction. The khalaf say: What is meant by rising is conquest and dominion. It is reported that a man asked Imam Malik ibn Anas, may Allah be pleased with him, about this verse, and he lowered his head for a long time, then said: 'The rising is not unknown, the modality is not comprehensible, belief in it is obligatory, questioning about it is an innovation, and I think you are nothing but misguided.' Then he ordered him to be taken out. And it is narrated that al-Zamakhshari asked al-Ghazali about this verse, and he answered him by saying: 'Since it is impossible for you to know yourself by a modality (kayfiyya) or a location (ayniyya), how is it fitting for your servitude that you describe Him, exalted, by a 'where' or a 'how', while He is sanctified above that?'

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the two methods for dealing with ambiguous texts (nusus muwhima) that seem to imply anthropomorphism: tafwīḍ (consigning the meaning to Allah without specifying) and ta'wīl (interpretation in a way befitting Allah). Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think istiwa' implies Allah is sitting on a throne.
Correction: Both salaf and khalaf agree Allah is not like creation; the salaf affirm the attribute without modality, and the khalaf interpret it as dominion.

Checkpoint
What was Imam Malik's attitude towards the questioner who asked about the 'how' of istiwa'?
A) He gave a detailed interpretation.
B) He said the inquiry is an innovation and ordered the man to be taken out.

D) He rebuked the man but then explained.

Key Takeaway
The istiwa' verse is handled by affirming the attribute while rejecting any anthropomorphic modality, with Imam Malik's response highlighting the danger of excessive questioning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse of istiwa', do you find yourself wanting to know 'how' it happens? What does Imam Malik's warning—'questioning about it is an innovation'—reveal about the state of your heart? Are you willing to submit to Allah's attributes without demanding explanations, even when your mind rebels? What would it cost you to simply affirm and move on?
?
Al-Ghazali uses the analogy of not knowing your own self by 'how' or 'where'. Have you ever truly reflected on the mystery of your own self—your soul, your consciousness? If you cannot comprehend your own essence, how can you presume to comprehend Allah's? What does this teach you about intellectual humility before your Lord? Will you let go of the need to grasp everything?
?
The man who asked Imam Malik was declared misguided and expelled. How does that make you feel? Are you afraid that your own questions about Allah might be signs of misguidance, or do you trust that your intentions are pure? How can you balance the pursuit of knowledge with the fear of exceeding proper bounds? Will you examine your questions to see if they stem from faith or from arrogance?
